\Hypertarget{classpandas_1_1core_1_1frame_1_1DataFrame_a9e0c6f0e9e9aa7cb1b1e191e481553d6}\index{pandas.core.frame.DataFrame@{pandas.core.frame.DataFrame}!unstack@{unstack}}
\index{unstack@{unstack}!pandas.core.frame.DataFrame@{pandas.core.frame.DataFrame}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{unstack()}{unstack()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classpandas_1_1core_1_1frame_1_1DataFrame_a9e0c6f0e9e9aa7cb1b1e191e481553d6} 
pandas.\+core.\+frame.\+Data\+Frame.\+unstack (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{, }\item[{Index\+Label }]{level}{ = {\ttfamily -\/1}, }\item[{}]{fill\+\_\+value}{ = {\ttfamily None}, }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{classpandas_1_1core_1_1generic_1_1NDFrame_abd03dfbde8c8a7808c464cd6dd26dfa4}{bool}} }]{sort}{ = {\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{classTrue}{True}}}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Pivot a level of the (necessarily hierarchical) index labels.

Returns a DataFrame having a new level of column labels whose inner-most level
consists of the pivoted index labels.

If the index is not a MultiIndex, the output will be a Series
(the analogue of stack when the columns are not a MultiIndex).

Parameters
----------
level : int, str, or list of these, default -1 (last level)
    Level(s) of index to unstack, can pass level name.
fill_value : int, str or dict
    Replace NaN with this value if the unstack produces missing values.
sort : bool, default True
    Sort the level(s) in the resulting MultiIndex columns.

Returns
-------
Series or DataFrame

See Also
--------
DataFrame.pivot : Pivot a table based on column values.
DataFrame.stack : Pivot a level of the column labels (inverse operation
    from `unstack`).

Notes
-----
Reference :ref:`the user guide <reshaping.stacking>` for more examples.

Examples
--------
>>> index = pd.MultiIndex.from_tuples([('one', 'a'), ('one', 'b'),
...                                    ('two', 'a'), ('two', 'b')])
>>> s = pd.Series(np.arange(1.0, 5.0), index=index)
>>> s
one  a   1.0
     b   2.0
two  a   3.0
     b   4.0
dtype: float64

>>> s.unstack(level=-1)
     a   b
one  1.0  2.0
two  3.0  4.0

>>> s.unstack(level=0)
   one  two
a  1.0   3.0
b  2.0   4.0

>>> df = s.unstack(level=0)
>>> df.unstack()
one  a  1.0
     b  2.0
two  a  3.0
     b  4.0
dtype: float64
\end{DoxyVerb}
 

Definition at line \mbox{\hyperlink{frame_8py_source_l09870}{9870}} of file \mbox{\hyperlink{frame_8py_source}{frame.\+py}}.



References \mbox{\hyperlink{generic_8py_source_l06256}{pandas.\+core.\+generic.\+NDFrame.\+\_\+\+\_\+finalize\+\_\+\+\_\+()}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{frame_8py_source_l00659}{\+\_\+constructor\+\_\+from\+\_\+mgr()}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{generic_8py_source_l00574}{pandas.\+core.\+generic.\+NDFrame.\+\_\+get\+\_\+axis\+\_\+number()}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{frame_8py_source_l00649}{\+\_\+mgr}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{featureVars_8py_source_l00533}{font\+Tools.\+var\+Lib.\+feature\+Vars.\+Shifter\+Visitor.\+shift}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{__mixins_8py_source_l00251}{pandas.\+core.\+arrays.\+\_\+mixins.\+NDArray\+Backed\+Extension\+Array.\+shift()}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{pandas_2core_2arrays_2base_8py_source_l01195}{pandas.\+core.\+arrays.\+base.\+Extension\+Array.\+shift()}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{arrays_2interval_8py_source_l01072}{pandas.\+core.\+arrays.\+interval.\+Interval\+Array.\+shift()}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{pandas_2core_2arrays_2sparse_2array_8py_source_l00811}{pandas.\+core.\+arrays.\+sparse.\+array.\+Sparse\+Array.\+shift()}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{frame_8py_source_l05870}{shift()}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{test__sampling_8py_source_l01330}{scipy.\+stats.\+tests.\+test\+\_\+sampling.\+Test\+Simple\+Ratio\+Uniforms.\+dist.\+shift}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{test__sampling_8py_source_l00472}{scipy.\+stats.\+tests.\+test\+\_\+sampling.\+Test\+Transformed\+Density\+Rejection.\+dist2.\+shift}}, and \mbox{\hyperlink{frame_8py_source_l09870}{unstack()}}.

\Hypertarget{classpandas_1_1core_1_1frame_1_1DataFrame_aa3449617311520d0567480a4dd5be7db}\index{pandas.core.frame.DataFrame@{pandas.core.frame.DataFrame}!update@{update}}
\index{update@{update}!pandas.core.frame.DataFrame@{pandas.core.frame.DataFrame}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{update()}{update()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classpandas_1_1core_1_1frame_1_1DataFrame_aa3449617311520d0567480a4dd5be7db} 
 None pandas.\+core.\+frame.\+Data\+Frame.\+update (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{, }\item[{}]{other}{, }\item[{Update\+Join }]{join}{ = {\ttfamily "{}left"{}}, }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{classpandas_1_1core_1_1generic_1_1NDFrame_abd03dfbde8c8a7808c464cd6dd26dfa4}{bool}} }]{overwrite}{ = {\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{classTrue}{True}}}, }\item[{}]{filter\+\_\+func}{ = {\ttfamily None}, }\item[{Ignore\+Raise }]{errors}{ = {\ttfamily "{}ignore"{}}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Modify in place using non-NA values from another DataFrame.

Aligns on indices. There is no return value.

Parameters
----------
other : DataFrame, or object coercible into a DataFrame
    Should have at least one matching index/column label
    with the original DataFrame. If a Series is passed,
    its name attribute must be set, and that will be
    used as the column name to align with the original DataFrame.
join : {'left'}, default 'left'
    Only left join is implemented, keeping the index and columns of the
    original object.
overwrite : bool, default True
    How to handle non-NA values for overlapping keys:

    * True: overwrite original DataFrame's values
      with values from `other`.
    * False: only update values that are NA in
      the original DataFrame.

filter_func : callable(1d-array) -> bool 1d-array, optional
    Can choose to replace values other than NA. Return True for values
    that should be updated.
errors : {'raise', 'ignore'}, default 'ignore'
    If 'raise', will raise a ValueError if the DataFrame and `other`
    both contain non-NA data in the same place.

Returns
-------
None
    This method directly changes calling object.

Raises
------
ValueError
    * When `errors='raise'` and there's overlapping non-NA data.
    * When `errors` is not either `'ignore'` or `'raise'`
NotImplementedError
    * If `join != 'left'`

See Also
--------
dict.update : Similar method for dictionaries.
DataFrame.merge : For column(s)-on-column(s) operations.

Examples
--------
>>> df = pd.DataFrame({'A': [1, 2, 3],
...                    'B': [400, 500, 600]})
>>> new_df = pd.DataFrame({'B': [4, 5, 6],
...                        'C': [7, 8, 9]})
>>> df.update(new_df)
>>> df
   A  B
0  1  4
1  2  5
2  3  6

The DataFrame's length does not increase as a result of the update,
only values at matching index/column labels are updated.

>>> df = pd.DataFrame({'A': ['a', 'b', 'c'],
...                    'B': ['x', 'y', 'z']})
>>> new_df = pd.DataFrame({'B': ['d', 'e', 'f', 'g', 'h', 'i']})
>>> df.update(new_df)
>>> df
   A  B
0  a  d
1  b  e
2  c  f

>>> df = pd.DataFrame({'A': ['a', 'b', 'c'],
...                    'B': ['x', 'y', 'z']})
>>> new_df = pd.DataFrame({'B': ['d', 'f']}, index=[0, 2])
>>> df.update(new_df)
>>> df
   A  B
0  a  d
1  b  y
2  c  f

For Series, its name attribute must be set.

>>> df = pd.DataFrame({'A': ['a', 'b', 'c'],
...                    'B': ['x', 'y', 'z']})
>>> new_column = pd.Series(['d', 'e', 'f'], name='B')
>>> df.update(new_column)
>>> df
   A  B
0  a  d
1  b  e
2  c  f

If `other` contains NaNs the corresponding values are not updated
in the original dataframe.

>>> df = pd.DataFrame({'A': [1, 2, 3],
...                    'B': [400., 500., 600.]})
>>> new_df = pd.DataFrame({'B': [4, np.nan, 6]})
>>> df.update(new_df)
>>> df
   A      B
0  1    4.0
1  2  500.0
2  3    6.0
\end{DoxyVerb}

\Hypertarget{classpandas_1_1core_1_1frame_1_1DataFrame_ad6c2920dd09f0443128988d1e59bad31}\index{pandas.core.frame.DataFrame@{pandas.core.frame.DataFrame}!value\_counts@{value\_counts}}
\index{value\_counts@{value\_counts}!pandas.core.frame.DataFrame@{pandas.core.frame.DataFrame}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{value\_counts()}{value\_counts()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classpandas_1_1core_1_1frame_1_1DataFrame_ad6c2920dd09f0443128988d1e59bad31} 
 \mbox{\hyperlink{classpandas_1_1core_1_1series_1_1Series}{Series}} pandas.\+core.\+frame.\+Data\+Frame.\+value\+\_\+counts (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{, }\item[{Index\+Label \texorpdfstring{$\vert$}{|} None }]{subset}{ = {\ttfamily None}, }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{classpandas_1_1core_1_1generic_1_1NDFrame_abd03dfbde8c8a7808c464cd6dd26dfa4}{bool}} }]{normalize}{ = {\ttfamily False}, }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{classpandas_1_1core_1_1generic_1_1NDFrame_abd03dfbde8c8a7808c464cd6dd26dfa4}{bool}} }]{sort}{ = {\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{classTrue}{True}}}, }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{classpandas_1_1core_1_1generic_1_1NDFrame_abd03dfbde8c8a7808c464cd6dd26dfa4}{bool}} }]{ascending}{ = {\ttfamily False}, }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{classpandas_1_1core_1_1generic_1_1NDFrame_abd03dfbde8c8a7808c464cd6dd26dfa4}{bool}} }]{dropna}{ = {\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{classTrue}{True}}}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Return a Series containing the frequency of each distinct row in the Dataframe.

Parameters
----------
subset : label or list of labels, optional
    Columns to use when counting unique combinations.
normalize : bool, default False
    Return proportions rather than frequencies.
sort : bool, default True
    Sort by frequencies when True. Sort by DataFrame column values when False.
ascending : bool, default False
    Sort in ascending order.
dropna : bool, default True
    Don't include counts of rows that contain NA values.

    .. versionadded:: 1.3.0

Returns
-------
Series

See Also
--------
Series.value_counts: Equivalent method on Series.

Notes
-----
The returned Series will have a MultiIndex with one level per input
column but an Index (non-multi) for a single label. By default, rows
that contain any NA values are omitted from the result. By default,
the resulting Series will be in descending order so that the first
element is the most frequently-occurring row.

Examples
--------
>>> df = pd.DataFrame({'num_legs': [2, 4, 4, 6],
...                    'num_wings': [2, 0, 0, 0]},
...                   index=['falcon', 'dog', 'cat', 'ant'])
>>> df
        num_legs  num_wings
falcon         2          2
dog            4          0
cat            4          0
ant            6          0

>>> df.value_counts()
num_legs  num_wings
4         0            2
2         2            1
6         0            1
Name: count, dtype: int64

>>> df.value_counts(sort=False)
num_legs  num_wings
2         2            1
4         0            2
6         0            1
Name: count, dtype: int64

>>> df.value_counts(ascending=True)
num_legs  num_wings
2         2            1
6         0            1
4         0            2
Name: count, dtype: int64

>>> df.value_counts(normalize=True)
num_legs  num_wings
4         0            0.50
2         2            0.25
6         0            0.25
Name: proportion, dtype: float64

With `dropna` set to `False` we can also count rows with NA values.

>>> df = pd.DataFrame({'first_name': ['John', 'Anne', 'John', 'Beth'],
...                    'middle_name': ['Smith', pd.NA, pd.NA, 'Louise']})
>>> df
  first_name middle_name
0       John       Smith
1       Anne        <NA>
2       John        <NA>
3       Beth      Louise

>>> df.value_counts()
first_name  middle_name
Beth        Louise         1
John        Smith          1
Name: count, dtype: int64

>>> df.value_counts(dropna=False)
first_name  middle_name
Anne        NaN            1
Beth        Louise         1
John        Smith          1
            NaN            1
Name: count, dtype: int64

>>> df.value_counts("first_name")
first_name
John    2
Anne    1
Beth    1
Name: count, dtype: int64
\end{DoxyVerb}
 

Reimplemented in \mbox{\hyperlink{classpandas_1_1core_1_1groupby_1_1generic_1_1DataFrameGroupBy_adf9f61b42b21ac8476a5f5fbb7946e68}{pandas.\+core.\+groupby.\+generic.\+Data\+Frame\+Group\+By}}.



Definition at line \mbox{\hyperlink{frame_8py_source_l07398}{7398}} of file \mbox{\hyperlink{frame_8py_source}{frame.\+py}}.



References \mbox{\hyperlink{varStore_8py_source_l00405}{font\+Tools.\+var\+Lib.\+var\+Store.\+\_\+\+Encoding.\+columns}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{apply_8py_source_l00876}{pandas.\+core.\+apply.\+Frame\+Apply.\+columns}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{frame_8py_source_l12553}{columns}}, and \mbox{\hyperlink{frame_8py_source_l09165}{groupby()}}.

\Hypertarget{classpandas_1_1core_1_1frame_1_1DataFrame_a44a6e7d641f118a610c52025803daabf}\index{pandas.core.frame.DataFrame@{pandas.core.frame.DataFrame}!values@{values}}
\index{values@{values}!pandas.core.frame.DataFrame@{pandas.core.frame.DataFrame}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{values()}{values()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classpandas_1_1core_1_1frame_1_1DataFrame_a44a6e7d641f118a610c52025803daabf} 
 np.\+ndarray pandas.\+core.\+frame.\+Data\+Frame.\+values (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Return a Numpy representation of the DataFrame.

.. warning::

   We recommend using :meth:`DataFrame.to_numpy` instead.

Only the values in the DataFrame will be returned, the axes labels
will be removed.

Returns
-------
numpy.ndarray
    The values of the DataFrame.

See Also
--------
DataFrame.to_numpy : Recommended alternative to this method.
DataFrame.index : Retrieve the index labels.
DataFrame.columns : Retrieving the column names.

Notes
-----
The dtype will be a lower-common-denominator dtype (implicit
upcasting); that is to say if the dtypes (even of numeric types)
are mixed, the one that accommodates all will be chosen. Use this
with care if you are not dealing with the blocks.

e.g. If the dtypes are float16 and float32, dtype will be upcast to
float32.  If dtypes are int32 and uint8, dtype will be upcast to
int32. By :func:`numpy.find_common_type` convention, mixing int64
and uint64 will result in a float64 dtype.

Examples
--------
A DataFrame where all columns are the same type (e.g., int64) results
in an array of the same type.

>>> df = pd.DataFrame({'age':    [ 3,  29],
...                    'height': [94, 170],
...                    'weight': [31, 115]})
>>> df
   age  height  weight
0    3      94      31
1   29     170     115
>>> df.dtypes
age       int64
height    int64
weight    int64
dtype: object
>>> df.values
array([[  3,  94,  31],
       [ 29, 170, 115]])

A DataFrame with mixed type columns(e.g., str/object, int64, float32)
results in an ndarray of the broadest type that accommodates these
mixed types (e.g., object).

>>> df2 = pd.DataFrame([('parrot',   24.0, 'second'),
...                     ('lion',     80.5, 1),
...                     ('monkey', np.nan, None)],
...                   columns=('name', 'max_speed', 'rank'))
>>> df2.dtypes
name          object
max_speed    float64
rank          object
dtype: object
>>> df2.values
array([['parrot', 24.0, 'second'],
       ['lion', 80.5, 1],
       ['monkey', nan, None]], dtype=object)
\end{DoxyVerb}
 

Reimplemented from \mbox{\hyperlink{classpandas_1_1core_1_1generic_1_1NDFrame}{pandas.\+core.\+generic.\+NDFrame}}.
